## Domain Knowledge
**Domain**: materials science / solid mechanics (thermo-mechanical constitutive modeling)
**Analysis**: The variables map directly to a thermo-mechanical constitutive law: stress (sigma) as a function of strain (epsilon) with temperature (T) affecting elastic moduli, thermal strain offsets, and plastic/viscoplastic flow stress (thermal softening or activation). Common structures include linear/nonlinear elasticity with temperature-dependent stiffness and thermally softened hardening laws.

**Common formula structures** (built-in generic + LLM domain-specific):
- Arrhenius equation: k = c0 * exp(c1 / T) (chemical reaction rate dependence on temperature)
- Coulomb's / Newton's inverse-square law: F = c0 / r**2 (gravitational or electrostatic force)
- Stefan-Boltzmann law: P = c0 * T**4 (blackbody radiation power vs temperature)
- Beer-Lambert law: I = c0 * exp(c1 * x) (light intensity attenuation through a medium)
- Michaelis-Menten kinetics: v = c0 * S / (S + c1) (enzyme-catalyzed reaction saturation)
- Hill equation: y = c0 * x**c1 / (x**c1 + c2) (cooperative binding, sigmoidal dose-response)
- Kepler's third law: T**2 = c0 * a**3 (orbital period vs semi-major axis)
- Newton's law of cooling: T = c0 + c1 * exp(c2 * t) (exponential thermal relaxation)
- Clausius-Clapeyron relation: log(P) = c0 + c1 / T (vapor pressure vs temperature)
- Langmuir adsorption isotherm: theta = c0 * P / (1 + c1 * P) (surface adsorption equilibrium)
- Freundlich isotherm: q = c0 * C**c1 (empirical adsorption on heterogeneous surface)
- Stokes' drag: F = c0 * r * v (viscous drag force on a sphere in fluid)
- Logistic growth: N = c0 / (1 + c1 * exp(c2 * t)) (population dynamics with carrying capacity)
- Planck-Wien approximation: I = c0 * f**3 * exp(c1 * f / T) (thermal radiation spectrum)
- Hooke’s law (isothermal linear elasticity): sigma = c0 * epsilon (small-strain elastic regime)
- Thermoelastic with thermal strain shift: sigma = c0 * (epsilon - c1 * (T - c2)) (stress from mechanical strain minus thermal expansion strain)
- Temperature-dependent modulus (linear-in-T): sigma = (c0 + c1 * T) * epsilon (elastic stiffness changes with temperature)
- Temperature-dependent modulus (reciprocal softening): sigma = c0 * epsilon / (T + c1) (modulus decreases with temperature)
- Nonlinear elastic polynomial: sigma = c0 * epsilon + c1 * epsilon**2 + c2 * epsilon**3 (moderate-strain elasticity / material nonlinearity)
- Odd-symmetric nonlinear elasticity: sigma = c0 * epsilon + c1 * Abs(epsilon)**c2 * Sign(epsilon) (tension-compression symmetric nonlinear response)
- Logarithmic (Hencky-like) strain law: sigma = c0 * log(c1 * epsilon + 1) (large-strain stiffening with reduced growth at small strain)
- Neo-Hookean-type uniaxial form (engineering strain via stretch): sigma = c0 * ((1 + epsilon) - (1 + epsilon)**(-2)) (rubber-like/hyperelastic response using stretch lambda = 1+epsilon)
- Entropic rubber elasticity with temperature scaling: sigma = c0 * T * ((1 + epsilon) - (1 + epsilon)**(-2)) (entropy-dominated elasticity proportional to temperature)
- Power-law hardening (Hollomon-like): sigma = c0 * Abs(epsilon)**c1 * Sign(epsilon) (plastic hardening after yield, rate-independent approximation)
- Thermally softened hardening: sigma = c0 * Abs(epsilon)**c1 * exp(c2 * T) * Sign(epsilon) (temperature-activated/softened flow stress; c2 often negative)
- Saturating/limited hardening with thermal scaling: sigma = (c0 * epsilon) / (1 + c1 * Abs(epsilon)) * (c2 + c3 * T) (hardening that approaches a limit, with temperature-dependent scale)
- Yield + hardening with thermal softening (piecewise cap): sigma = Min(c0 * epsilon, (c1 + c2 * Abs(epsilon)**c3) * exp(c4 * T)) * Sign(epsilon) (elastic then plastic with temperature-dependent flow stress)

**Formula structure heuristic features**:
- Oscillation damping envelope → Exponential decay envelope f(x)*exp(-c*Abs(x)) for symmetric damped oscillation, Gaussian envelope f(x)*exp(-c*x**2) for localized wave packets
- Saturation/clipping effects → Rational fraction x/(1+x), tanh; for variables with alternating positive/negative in oscillatory systems, selectively apply Abs
- Growth/decay → Exponential growth exp(c*t), Logistic 1/(1+exp(-c*x)), power law x**c
- Threshold/activation behavior → Max(x-c, 0), piecewise functions
- Coupling/cross effects → Product terms between variables x*y, power-law coupling x**c1 * y**c2
- Elastic stiffness typically decreases with increasing T → use (c0 + c1 * T) multipliers or reciprocal forms c0/(T+c1) multiplying epsilon.
- Thermal expansion appears as an additive strain offset → model sigma as proportional to (epsilon - c * (T - T0)).
- Large-strain kinematics often involve stretch (1 + epsilon) rather than epsilon alone → include (1+epsilon) and negative powers like (1+epsilon)**(-2).
- Plastic hardening commonly follows a power law in strain magnitude → include Abs(epsilon)**n with Sign(epsilon) to preserve odd symmetry.
- Thermal softening/activation of flow stress is frequently exponential in T (or in homologous temperature) → include exp(c * T) factors (with c often negative).
- Materials often show an initial linear elastic region transitioning to nonlinear hardening → use Min/Max (piecewise) between c*epsilon and a hardening branch.
- To prevent unbounded stress growth at high strain in empirical fits, use saturating rational forms like epsilon/(1 + c*Abs(epsilon)).
- For moderate strains, logarithmic dependence on (1 + c*epsilon) can capture gradual stiffening without excessive curvature at small strain.
- If tension/compression behavior is approximately symmetric, enforce odd symmetry via Sign(epsilon) and functions of Abs(epsilon).
